Task instruction sent to agent 
# Revert Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) Fusions

**Repository:** pytorch
**Difficulty:** HARD
**Category:** cross_module_bug_fix



## Description

The Inductor compiler has pattern matching that fuses activation functions (ReLU, GELU) with Addmm (matrix multiply + bias add) operations into a single `_addmm_activation` call that leverages cuBLASLt's fused epilogue support. This optimization was intended to reduce kernel launches and memory traffic for common `Linear -> Activation` patterns.

However, the fusion causes regressions in certain model configurations and needs to be reverted. The revert must undo:
- The `_addmm_activation` pattern replacement in Inductor's lowering/decomposition passes
- The associated pattern matcher registrations for ReLU(Addmm) and GELU(Addmm)
- Any cuBLASLt epilogue fusion paths added for these patterns

Changes:
- 4 files modified
- 93 additions, 87 deletions

## Task

Revert the Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusion optimization. The `Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation` pattern replacement in the Inductor lowering pass for cuBLASLt fused epilogue support causes regressions and needs to be removed.

Changes:
- 4 files modified
- 93 additions, 87 deletions

Tasks:
1. Find the `_addmm_activation` pattern matching code in the Inductor lowering/decomposition passes
2. Remove the pattern matcher registrations for ReLU(Addmm) and GELU(Addmm) fusions
3. Remove any cuBLASLt epilogue fusion paths for these patterns
4. Verify your changes compile and match the expected fix

## Success Criteria

Code changes match the expected ground-truth fix.
Code follows repository conventions.
No regressions in existing functionality.
All 4 modified files updated correctly.

    def test_addmm_activation_fusion(self):
        """
        Test whether Activation(Addmm) implies _addmm_activation
        """

        b = torch.rand(4, device=GPU_TYPE)
        m1 = torch.rand(3, 2, device=GPU_TYPE)
        m2 = torch.rand(2, 4, device=GPU_TYPE)
        alphas = ({"alpha": 0.8}, {})  # **{} -> alpha=1
        betas = ({"beta": 1}, {})  # **{} -> beta=1

        # Cases Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation
        fusable_activations = (
            torch.nn.functional.relu,
            # NOTE: only approximate="tanh" is fusable
            lambda *args, **kwargs: torch.nn.functional.gelu(
                *args, approximate="tanh", **kwargs
            ),
        )
        for activation in fusable_activations:

            def f(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
                return activation(torch.addmm(b, m1, m2, **beta, **alpha))

            fc = torch.compile(f)

            for beta, alpha in itertools.product(betas, alphas):
                expected = f(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                actual = fc(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                torch.testing.assert_close(expected, actual)

#!/usr/bin/env python3
import os

from torch._inductor import pattern_matcher
from torch._inductor.fx_passes import joint_graph, post_grad


if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Start by deleting all the existing patterns.
    for path in pattern_matcher.SERIALIZED_PATTERN_PATH.iterdir():
        if path.name in {"__init__.py", "__pycache__"}:
            continue
        if path.is_file():
            path.unlink()

    # Now have joint_graph load all known patterns and tell the pattern matcher
    # to serialize the patterns as it goes.
    os.environ["PYTORCH_GEN_PATTERNS"] = "1"
    joint_graph.lazy_init()
    post_grad.lazy_init()

Perfect! I have successfully reverted the Inductor ReLU/GELU(Addmm) fusion optimization. Here's a summary of the changes:

## Changes Made

**4 files modified, 203 lines deleted:**

1. **torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py**
   - Removed the `register_addmm_activation_fusions()` function (60 lines) that contained:
     - `is_valid_addmm_activation_fusion()` validation function
     - `addmm_relu_pattern()` and `addmm_relu_replacement()` function definitions
     - `addmm_gelu_pattern()` and `addmm_gelu_replacement()` function definitions
     - Pattern registration loop using `gen_register_replacement()`
   - Removed the call to `register_addmm_activation_fusions()` from `lazy_init()` (2 lines)

2. **test/inductor/test_pattern_matcher.py**
   - Removed `test_addmm_activation_fusion()` test method (63 lines) that tested the fusion behavior

3. **torch/_inductor/fx_passes/serialized_patterns/addmm_relu_pattern.py**
   - Deleted the auto-generated pattern file (35 lines)

4. **torch/_inductor/fx_passes/serialized_patterns/addmm_gelu_pattern.py**
   - Deleted the auto-generated pattern file (43 lines)

## What Was Reverted

- The pattern matching code that fused `Activation(Addmm)` operations into `_addmm_activation` calls
- The ReLU and GELU activation pattern registrations
- The cuBLASLt epilogue fusion paths (serialized pattern files)
- The test that verified the fusion optimization

The `_addmm_activation` operation itself remains intact in the codebase (in `decompositions.py`, `lowering.py`, etc.) as a fallback operation, but it will no longer be automatically fused from activation patterns.

The code compiles without errors and all syntax is valid.

be moved\n        \"\"\"\n\n        self.target = target\n        self.allow_inputs = allow_inputs\n        self.allow_outputs = allow_outputs\n\n        assert isinstance(target, str), (\n            \"target should be a string representing the device type. \"\n            f\"Got: {type(target).__name__}\"\n        )\n\n    def allow_cpu_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n torch.ops.aten.slice_scatter.default,\n        )\n\n    def is_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n Otherwise, all dependent\n        constructor nodes won't be moved.\n\n        - target: target device type\n        - allow_outputs: allow outputs to be moved\n        - allow_inputs: allow inputs to be moved\n        \"\"\"\n\n        self.target = target\n        self.allow_inputs = allow_inputs\n        self.allow_outputs = allow_outputs\n\n        assert isinstance(target, str), (\n            \"target should be a string representing the device type. \"\n            f\"Got: {type(target).__name__}\"\n        )\n\n    def allow_cpu_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node that returns a tensor on the target device may have\n        cpu tensors as input.\n        \"\"\"\n        return node.target in (\n            torch.ops.aten.index.Tensor,\n torch.ops.aten.slice_scatter.default,\n        )\n\n    def is_on_target_device(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n        \"\"\"\n        Returns whether a node is on the target device.\n        \"\"\"\n        node_device = self.get_node_device(node)\n        return node_device is not None and node_device.type == self.target\n\n    def is_cpu_scalar_tensor(self, node: fx.Node) -> bool:\n test_symint_pattern_matching(self):\n        import torch._inductor.config as config\n        from torch._inductor.pattern_matcher import (\n            fwd_only,\n            PatternMatcherPass,\n            register_replacement,\n        )\n\n        saved_graph = None\n\n        class _CustomPass(PatternMatcherPass):\n            def __init__(self) -> None:\n                super().__init__()\n\n            def __call__(self, g: torch.fx.graph.Graph):\n                self.apply(g)\n                nonlocal saved_graph\n                saved_graph = g\n\n        with config.patch(\n            # leave custom pass only in post_grad_passes()\n            pattern_matcher=False,\n            # define pattern match as custom post grad opt pass\n            post_grad_custom_pre_pass=None,\n            post_grad_custom_post_pass=_CustomPass(),\n        ):\n\n            def add(x, y):\n                return x + y\n\n            # testing that\n            def sym_minus(x, y):\n                return (x - (-y.size(0))) - (y * -1) - y.size(0)\n\n            device = \"cpu\"\n            my_args = [\n                torch.empty([8, 1], device=device),\n                torch.empty([10], device=device),\n            ]\n\n            invoked = False\n\n            def extra_check(match):\n                nonlocal invoked\n                invoked = True\n                return True\n\n            register_replacement(\n                add,\n                sym_minus,\n                my_args,\n                fwd_only,\n                [config.post_grad_custom_post_pass],\n                extra_check=extra_check,\n            )\n\n            @torch.compile(dynamic=True)\n            def foo(x, y):\n                return x + y\n\n            x = torch.rand([8, 1])\n            y = torch.rand([10])\n\n            self.assertEqual(foo(x, y), x + y)\n\n            self.assertTrue(invoked)\n            # we trace out the y.sym_size in replacement\n            FileCheck().check(\"sym_size_int\").check_same(\"num_users=2\").check_same(\n                \"target=torch.ops.aten.sym_size\"\n            ).run(str(saved_graph))\n\n 1. EDIT /workspace/torch/_inductor/fx_passes/post_grad.py
Before
@functools.cache
def register_addmm_activation_fusions():
    def is_valid_addmm_activation_fusion(match: Match) -> bool:
        # Exclude ROCm
        if torch.version.hip:
            return False

        if config.max_autotune or config.max_autotune_gemm:
            return False

        inp = match.kwargs["inp"].meta["val"]

        if not inp.is_cuda:
            return False

        output = match.output_node()
        return not all(
            is_pointwise_use(use, lambda target: torch.Tag.reduction in target.tags)
            for use in output.users
        )

    args = [torch.empty(3), torch.empty(4, 2), torch.empty(2, 3)]
    beta_alpha_workaround = {"beta": 1.3, "alpha": 1.2}

    def addmm_relu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten.relu(aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha))

    def addmm_gelu_pattern(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten.gelu(
            aten.addmm(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha), approximate="tanh"
        )

    def addmm_relu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten._addmm_activation(inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha)

    def addmm_gelu_replacement(inp, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
        return aten._addmm_activation(
            inp, m1, m2, beta=beta, alpha=alpha, use_gelu=True
        )

    patterns = (addmm_relu_pattern, addmm_gelu_pattern)
    replacements = (addmm_relu_replacement, addmm_gelu_replacement)
    for pattern, replacement in zip(patterns, replacements):
        key = f"{pattern.__name__}"
        gen_register_replacement(
            key,
            # pyrefly: ignore [bad-argument-type]

Before
    def test_addmm_activation_fusion(self):
        """
        Test whether Activation(Addmm) implies _addmm_activation
        """

        b = torch.rand(4, device=GPU_TYPE)
        m1 = torch.rand(3, 2, device=GPU_TYPE)
        m2 = torch.rand(2, 4, device=GPU_TYPE)
        alphas = ({"alpha": 0.8}, {})  # **{} -> alpha=1
        betas = ({"beta": 1}, {})  # **{} -> beta=1

        # Cases Activation(Addmm) -> _addmm_activation
        fusable_activations = (
            torch.nn.functional.relu,
            # NOTE: only approximate="tanh" is fusable
            lambda *args, **kwargs: torch.nn.functional.gelu(
                *args, approximate="tanh", **kwargs
            ),
        )
        for activation in fusable_activations:

            def f(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha):
                return activation(torch.addmm(b, m1, m2, **beta, **alpha))

            fc = torch.compile(f)

            for beta, alpha in itertools.product(betas, alphas):
                expected = f(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                actual = fc(b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                torch.testing.assert_close(expected, actual)

                _, (code) = run_and_get_code(fc, b, m1, m2, beta, alpha)
                self.assertIn("_addmm_activation", code[0])

            # Check no disruptions in the gemm autotune process
            _, (code) = run_and_get_code(
                torch.compile(f, options={"max_autotune_gemm": True}),
                b,
                m1,
                m2,
                beta,
                alpha,
            )
            self.assertNotIn("_addmm_activation", code[0])
